  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>Selecting / projecting a column whose value is represented as a stream more than once crashes Derby, i.e.:<br> ResultSet rs = stmt.executeQuery("SELECT clobValue AS clobOne, clobValue AS clobTwo FROM mytable");<br> rs.getString(1);<br> rs.getString(2);</p> 
                  <p>After having looked at the class of bugs having to do with reuse of stream data types, I now have a possible fix. It fixes <a href="https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DERBY-3645" title="Insert into selecting BLOB column twice leads to SQLException: Restore of a serializable or SQLData object of class error selecting from the table" class="issue-link" data-issue-key="DERBY-3645"><del>DERBY-3645</del></a>, <a href="https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DERBY-3646" title="Embedded returns wrong results when selecting a blob column twice and using getBinaryStream()" class="issue-link" data-issue-key="DERBY-3646"><del>DERBY-3646</del></a> and <a href="https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DERBY-2349" title="Accessing a BLOB column twice in an INSERT trigger leads to errors in the value on-disk" class="issue-link" data-issue-key="DERBY-2349"><del>DERBY-2349</del></a> (there may be more Jiras).<br> The core of the fix is cloning certain DVDs being selected/projected in multiple columns. There are two types of cloning:<br> A) materializing clone<br> B) stream clone</p> 
                  <p>(A) can be implemented already, (B) requires code to clone a stream without materializing it. Note that the streams I'm talking about are streams originating from the store.</p> 
                  <p>Testing revealed the following:</p> 
                  <ul class="alternate" type="square"> 
                   <li>the cost of the checks performed to figure out if cloning is required seems acceptable (negligible?)</li> 
                   <li>in some cases (A) has better performance than (B) because the raw data only has to be decoded once</li> 
                   <li>stream clones are preferred when the data value is above a certain size for several reasons:</li> 
                  </ul> 
                  <ul> 
                   <li>avoids potential out-of-memory errors (and in case of a server environment, it lowers the memory pressure)</li> 
                   <li>avoids decoding the whole value if the JDBC streaming APIs are used to access only parts of the value</li> 
                   <li>avoids decoding overall in cases where the value isn't accessed by the client / user<br> (this statement conflicts with the performance observation above)</li> 
                  </ul> 
                  <p>We don't always know the size of a value, and since the fix code deals with all kinds of data types, it is slightly more costly to try to obtain the size.</p> 
                  <p>What do people think about the following goal statement?<br> Goals:<br> ----- Phase 1<br> 1) No crashes or wrong results due to stream reuse when executing duplicate column selections (minus goal 4)<br> 2) Minimal performance degradation for non-duplicate column selections<br> 3) Only a minor performance degradation for duplicate [<span class="error">[LONG]</span> VAR]CHAR <span class="error">[FOR BIT DATA]</span> column selections<br> ----- Phase 2<br> 4) No out-of-memory exceptions during execution of duplicate column selections of BLOB/CLOB<br> 5) Optimize BLOB/CLOB cloning</p> 
                  <p>I think phase 1 can proceed by reviewing and discussing the prototype patch. Phase 2 requires more discussion and work (see <a href="https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DERBY-3650" title="internal multiple references from different rows to a single BLOB/CLOB stream leads to various errors when second reference used." class="issue-link" data-issue-key="DERBY-3650"><del>DERBY-3650</del></a>).</p> 
                  <p>A note about the bug behavior facts:<br> Since this issue is the underlying cause for several other reported issues, I have decided to be liberal when setting the bug behavior facts. Depending on where the duplicate column selection is used, it can cause both crashes, wrong results and data corruption.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>
